<script>
  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_b33332ce-0202-43b5-a80d-00c5e12038ed'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);
    };
    if (typeof AppleID !== "undefined") {
      initAppleId();
    } else {
      initializeSiwa();
    }

</script>

  <span id="freeText2354017189659719630" style="display:none">The perfect gift for fans of "The Hunger Games" and " Divergent," this boxed set includes all of the paperback editions of James Dashner's" New York Times" bestselling series"--The Maze Runner," "The Scorch Trials," "The Death Cure" and "The Kill Order."<br /><br />When Thomas wakes up in the lift, the only thing he can remember is his name. It's the only way out--and no one's ever made it through alive. <br />"Everything is going to change." <br /> Then a girl arrives. The first girl ever. And the message she delivers is terrifying. <br /> Remember. Survive. Run.</span>

<span class='communityAnswerText'>
<span class="expandableContainer"><span class="truncatedContent">Yes. Saw the movies first and just finished the books one after another which is always a great plan! The writing was such that I was able to get into<a class="jsShow showAction" href="#">…more</a></span><span class="fullContent">Yes. Saw the movies first and just finished the books one after another which is always a great plan! The writing was such that I was able to get into the characters &amp; the story line easily. They will not be easily forgotten which often happens with other books. I'm a senior citizen who loves to read and tries to keep up with what my grandchildren enjoy! Lovely experience. <a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>
</span>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2500038758?book_show_action=true">Aug 27, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Aishu Rehman" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Aishu Rehman" href="/user/show/73221135-aishu-rehman">Aishu Rehman</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/23342511-the-maze-runner-series">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2500038758" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1542044057142359736">The Maze Runner doesn't match competitors in the genre like The Hunger Games and Divergence, but it isn't terrible either. It is really rather more of the same - though the concept is compelling, the author fails to fully deliver and you end up with a watered down version of a Westerfeld novel (no one can touch the brilliance of Uglies so I'd rather they stop trying).<br/><br/>There are a few traps Dashner is guilty of here that I wish authors would stop falling for. First, the main character is rather wh</span>
  <span id="freeText1542044057142359736" style="display:none">The Maze Runner doesn't match competitors in the genre like The Hunger Games and Divergence, but it isn't terrible either. It is really rather more of the same - though the concept is compelling, the author fails to fully deliver and you end up with a watered down version of a Westerfeld novel (no one can touch the brilliance of Uglies so I'd rather they stop trying).<br /><br />There are a few traps Dashner is guilty of here that I wish authors would stop falling for. First, the main character is rather whiny. I have no idea why that's a thing, but it takes away from a character. Second, advancing the plot by having characters not speak to each other, so they end up in a crisis. boring. Third, unnecessarily creating a new sublanguage (the only one of these I ever liked was in Uglies).</span>
  <a data-text-id="1542044057142359736" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1008552919" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1008552919" />
    <a title="Kerry Ann" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5620709-kerry-ann"><img alt="Kerry Ann" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1405883974p2/5620709.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1008552919?book_show_action=true">Jul 27, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kerry Ann" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kerry Ann" href="/user/show/5620709-kerry-ann">Kerry Ann</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1008552919" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13353004720613667330">Most low reviews I read expressed disappointment, let down expecting a similarity with other near-future teen-lit (Hunger Games, Divergent). I ignored those reviews. Having not read these other books and seeking a fast paced mindless weekend read I felt confident disappointment would not be my fate. <br/><br/>I pen this rare review to save the next unsuspecting reader. <br/><br/>This author has lazing writing habits. Something that can be forgiven if the plot is fast paced and well developed. It was not. <br/><br/>Lazy writi</span>
  <span id="freeText13353004720613667330" style="display:none">Most low reviews I read expressed disappointment, let down expecting a similarity with other near-future teen-lit (Hunger Games, Divergent). I ignored those reviews. Having not read these other books and seeking a fast paced mindless weekend read I felt confident disappointment would not be my fate. <br /><br />I pen this rare review to save the next unsuspecting reader. <br /><br />This author has lazing writing habits. Something that can be forgiven if the plot is fast paced and well developed. It was not. <br /><br />Lazy writing –author tells you, does not show you. I skimmed passed large portions of the book where the author regularly inserted a character sole for the purpose of delivering a speech/explanation. The action does not speak for itself. Key characters go under developed; I never could come to care about them. <br /><br />I've enjoyed books penned by lazy author. Those plots were interesting and believable. Things were reviled at such a pace that you felt like you were on an exciting ride, wanting more. This author quickly loses the thread of believability. Felt like a Hollywood action sequel, sad knock off where explosions and gore are used to distract from the poor acting and sub par plot. <br /><br />If you seek a good read I recommend passing this selection up for another.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="13353004720613667330" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText4862426219715125830" style="display:none">This book passed it predecessor by far!<br /><br />The second book in the maze runner series meet my expectation and over! The book takes place right where the last book took place which I loved. This book set the gladers up with an amazing trial full of dangers, secrets, suspense and betrayal. What I loved about thee book is that there was so much more action in this book then in the last one and that's something that I really liked. Also the plot I feel was much better then the first book because the writer just straight up tells you what's going on and not just placing you in a strange maze without knowing what's going on.<br /><br />I also really liked the characters this time around. I loved the friendship between Thomas, Minho and Newt. And I also loved reading about Thomas's and Theresa's relationship which I couldn't get enough of. I also wanted to get to know the new characters Aris and Brenda.<br /><br />Over all this book is suspenseful and if full of plot twist that will break your hearts. </span>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1070425771" />
    <a title="Ricardo Basallo" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/24826970-ricardo-basallo"><img alt="Ricardo Basallo" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1382226870p2/24826970.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1070425771?book_show_action=true">Oct 02, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ricardo Basallo" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ricardo Basallo" href="/user/show/24826970-ricardo-basallo">Ricardo Basallo</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1070425771" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14140665493826271237">I can't help but notice the many parallels the series has with The Hunger Games. Thomas reads like a male Katniss Everdeen:<br/><br/>1. Protagonist is a teenager who has lost a parent<br/>2. Story is set in a dystopic world and even mentions a location that both series share<br/>3. Protagonist is thrown into many life and death situations along with people his age<br/>4. Protagonist has both witnessed and committed acts which would scar any person for life<br/>5. Protagonist becomes a symbol of rebellion and fights against a</span>
  <span id="freeText14140665493826271237" style="display:none">I can't help but notice the many parallels the series has with The Hunger Games. Thomas reads like a male Katniss Everdeen:<br /><br />1. Protagonist is a teenager who has lost a parent<br />2. Story is set in a dystopic world and even mentions a location that both series share<br />3. Protagonist is thrown into many life and death situations along with people his age<br />4. Protagonist has both witnessed and committed acts which would scar any person for life<br />5. Protagonist becomes a symbol of rebellion and fights against an authority composed of adults<br />6. Protagonist finds peace in the end but not before suffering a most tragic loss<br /><br /><br />What I like about the series are that:<br /><br />1. While the first few chapters can be dragging, once it gets going the books are hard to put down. <br />2. The series is very coherent and each book is important in delivering the story as a whole. No one book is better than the rest.<br /><br />But essentially it's the same young adult story but packaged differently so if you're in the market to read about teenagers who act beyond their age in extraordinary and terrible circumstances, Maze Runner is a good pick for you.</span>
  <a data-text-id="14140665493826271237" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1042722058" />
    <a title="Rory" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1472215-rory"><img alt="Rory" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1423006208p2/1472215.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1042722058?book_show_action=true">Sep 01, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Rory" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Rory" href="/user/show/1472215-rory">Rory</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1042722058" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18330143804810117009">I have many contradictory opinions about this series but these are the highlights without giving any of the plot away.<br/><br/>- The 1st book in the series is a bit slow. The author tries to make it mysterious but really he just drags things out too much. I am happy to report that I just watched the movie and they fixed a lot of the problems the 1st book had like the slow pace and the author’s tendency to make things overly complex. <br/><br/>- I also was never fully satisfied for the reasoning behind the Maze. Th</span>
  <span id="freeText18330143804810117009" style="display:none">I have many contradictory opinions about this series but these are the highlights without giving any of the plot away.<br /><br />- The 1st book in the series is a bit slow. The author tries to make it mysterious but really he just drags things out too much. I am happy to report that I just watched the movie and they fixed a lot of the problems the 1st book had like the slow pace and the author’s tendency to make things overly complex. <br /><br />- I also was never fully satisfied for the reasoning behind the Maze. The author never goes into any explanation as to how the purpose behind the Maze gets to the goal it apparently was designed for (that is all I can say without giving anything away).<br /><br />- The 2nd and 3rd books are all action. This makes them really fast reads but they start to get monotonous. In my opinion, a good book should go somewhere, have some kind of climax, but this series just tries to ride the adrenaline high of the characters until the very end. <br /><br />- Also, this series is very very dark. It made the hunger games look like a picture perfect society comparatively. I found that by the end of the 2nd book, I was tired of this horrible world, all the dying, and the non-stop action.<br /><br />I gave these books 3 stars because for the most part it kept me entertained, but I would not recommend this series to a child or the faint of heart. If you really stop and consider the world the author has created, then you cannot help but to be horrified.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="18330143804810117009" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_1098039602" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1098039602" />
    <a title="David" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/32976914-david"><img alt="David" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1407506006p2/32976914.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1098039602?book_show_action=true">Nov 05, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="David" class="user" itemprop="url" name="David" href="/user/show/32976914-david">David</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1098039602" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13244271206773934545">Yet another trilogy in the style of <i>The Hunger Games</i> and <i>Divergent</i>. It has been advertised as such and I would agree. The complete series also includes a prequel which I think worked well in explaining the origins of the world the Maze Runner is set in. The story is stranger (for lack of a better word) and the premise not as strong as <i>The Hunger Games</i> and <i>Divergent</i> but the trilogy as a whole is much stronger, and does not taper out in the later books as the other trilogies did. It was a much mor</span>
  <span id="freeText13244271206773934545" style="display:none">Yet another trilogy in the style of <i>The Hunger Games</i> and <i>Divergent</i>. It has been advertised as such and I would agree. The complete series also includes a prequel which I think worked well in explaining the origins of the world the Maze Runner is set in. The story is stranger (for lack of a better word) and the premise not as strong as <i>The Hunger Games</i> and <i>Divergent</i> but the trilogy as a whole is much stronger, and does not taper out in the later books as the other trilogies did. It was a much more consistent experience.<br /><br />Plot progression was good, the books are fast-paced and difficult to put down, and I always wanted to know what happened next. The setting is vastly different in every book and is pretty well described and helps set the scenes of desperation in the dystopian world. Character development in the main trilogy is poor. Interesting characters had the unfortunate tendency to die, while the main characters do not seem to progress past a "rebel with a cause" persona. It was better in the prequel. I also did not really buy into the premise of mapping the brain's reaction to different variables as a way to find a cure to a disease, seemed silly to my scientific mind.<br /><br />Overall, worth the read and kept me entertained on the 40 hours flying to London and back.</span>
  <a data-text-id="13244271206773934545" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer7032648471268485971">The Maze Runner series By James Dashner is very hard to follow at times because it begins in the middle finishes and then goes back to the beginning. In a dystopian society where sun flares destroyed the world and then a deadly virus came and wiped out all but a small sample of immune children. WCKD takes the children and puts them in trials to try and find a cure. It turns out that there is no cure so the children rebel and are taken through more tests. In the end, they do find a small paradise</span>
  <span id="freeText7032648471268485971" style="display:none">The Maze Runner series By James Dashner is very hard to follow at times because it begins in the middle finishes and then goes back to the beginning. In a dystopian society where sun flares destroyed the world and then a deadly virus came and wiped out all but a small sample of immune children. WCKD takes the children and puts them in trials to try and find a cure. It turns out that there is no cure so the children rebel and are taken through more tests. In the end, they do find a small paradise and lock themselves in so that none of the non-immune can get them. I like that he wrote the books in the order he did or the whole story would have been given away in the beginning. I do not like that a lot of the main characters die in some way to help others escape. If you want to read this book you should like science fiction. I would highly recommend this series. <br /><br /></span>

<div id="review_1755879008" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1755879008" />
    <a title="Sydney J" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/59561771-sydney-j"><img alt="Sydney J" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/u_50x66-632230dc9882b4352d753eedf9396530.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1755879008?book_show_action=true">Sep 12, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sydney J" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sydney J" href="/user/show/59561771-sydney-j">Sydney J</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1755879008" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3924661115272770682">Maze Runner<br/><br/> Thomas will soon wake up with no memory, no thoughts and no ideas. Who knows what was waiting for him, after all he was in a metal box surrounded by darkness. When the boys pulled him up he felt strangely at home...what did this mean? The day right after a girl arrived in the dank, dark box. But a new boy comes every two weeks. Why would a girl come the day right after a new boy had arrived? Realizing there had to be a way out of the maze he sets off looking for the hidden exit. He d</span>
  <span id="freeText3924661115272770682" style="display:none">Maze Runner<br /><br /> Thomas will soon wake up with no memory, no thoughts and no ideas. Who knows what was waiting for him, after all he was in a metal box surrounded by darkness. When the boys pulled him up he felt strangely at home...what did this mean? The day right after a girl arrived in the dank, dark box. But a new boy comes every two weeks. Why would a girl come the day right after a new boy had arrived? Realizing there had to be a way out of the maze he sets off looking for the hidden exit. He discovers secrets that lie underneath another, he will run into trouble and will have a special ability to talk to that strange girl in his head. But it's all worth it when they escape. This first book is alive with imagery and vivid words. It made me feel as if I, myself was stuck in the box. This book is good for <u>Divergent</u> lovers and <u>Hunger Games</u> fans.<br /><br />Scorch Trials<br /><br /> They escaped from WICKED, they witnessed the worst of humanity. They are now safe from the wicked world. Turns out the trials are not over, it's time for things to become harder, deadlier. Inhaled and spit out in the desert with scorching sand and a blazing sun, there's no way that the boys can make it. But they escaped from the maze, they defied all logics. They have two weeks to make it across 100 miles of desert. When they're about to sleep a wail wakes them up and the find Teresa and she warns Thomas. She was right he would go through unthinkable terrors of love and relationships. Of course he meets another girl but how will Thomas decide? When they reach the "safe haven" they know that WICKED is planning something, something big. This book is like the <u>Maze Runner</u> just with a twist of defiance, and sprinkle of romance and more mysteries. You'll love this book no matter what.<br /><br />Death Cure<br /><br /> Alive and escaping, and now on the way to Denver, Thomas is still surprised that he worked with WICKED. Still retrieving memories from his past they continue forward, looking for Teresa and his friends that supposedly left him behind. With the help of Newt, Minho, Jorge, and Brenda they try to find the person that gave them a note, the note that was written by a past enemy. Once they found him they got the devices in their brains out but before that Thomas almost killed the man that made the procedure. Roaming around with almost a close capture with WICKED they have no choice but to run. Something odd was happening and on that same odd day they were kidnapped, but not by a bounty hunter(WICKED had set a huge bounty), but by the Right Arm. Turned out that all their friends had been taken in by the Right Arm. The Rebellious group has a plan, a plan that will end all the destruction that WICKED created. Thomas is the missing piece to WICKED though, well his brain is.... So as they try but Chancellor Paige stops them and tries to save all the immunes but the only way for that to happen is if he goes back into the maze. The maze that holds truths and lies. Thomas has to lead all the immunes out of the maze with a map and a new maze that has an end, the end that leads to freedom. With love and loss he finds himself with Brenda knowing full well that Teresa would want him to be happy. This is the best conclusion to a book series ever! I loved when he has to go back in the maze, I thought I was in it my self. Again if you liked the first and second of this series than you'll love this book.</span>
  <a data-text-id="3924661115272770682" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1204480867" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1204480867" />
    <a title="Amy" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/34590384-amy"><img alt="Amy" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1578174406p2/34590384.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1204480867?book_show_action=true">Feb 18, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Amy" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Amy" href="/user/show/34590384-amy">Amy</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1204480867" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8273243179063041092">When I finished this series, I had one thought: finally. (As in, yay, I'm finally done.) I literally do not understand at all why this series is so popular. For one thing, it is so badly and lazily written. The writing is filled with clichés. Oh, and speaking of the word "filled" ... that is one of Dashner's favorite words in the entire world. I cannot tell you the amount of times something "filled the air" or "filled Thomas's mind." And "filled" is not the only word that is FAR overused in this</span>
  <span id="freeText8273243179063041092" style="display:none">When I finished this series, I had one thought: finally. (As in, yay, I'm finally done.) I literally do not understand at all why this series is so popular. For one thing, it is so badly and lazily written. The writing is filled with clichés. Oh, and speaking of the word "filled" ... that is one of Dashner's favorite words in the entire world. I cannot tell you the amount of times something "filled the air" or "filled Thomas's mind." And "filled" is not the only word that is FAR overused in this book. Everything is just so awkwardly and often unnecessarily worded. The "cool" (aka, stupid and annoying) slang that the characters use grated on my nerves so much that I could hardly stand it. And every attempt to be funny or witty fails miserably...every joke sounds like something that my 10 year old brother would make to try to impress his older siblings. They're just...not funny.<br />Every character is horribly underdeveloped. I honestly didn't care about any of the characters at all... We are TOLD why we like characters, not SHOWN why we like then. (Which basically means...I didn't like them. I didn't care if they died. I didn't care if they were upset.) Thomas does not grow as a character at all from the first sentence to the last of the series...he always stays the same boring, lifeless, unrealistic boy. I didn't understand why Thomas liked people either...Thomas will think about someone as his best friend in the world...but I had no idea why, because I was never shown any relationship development at all. <br />On top of all of this, I honestly just thought that the plot was stale. I was so bored. Just when I thought that something cool might happen, I was disappointed as a new "reveal" turned out to be just another boring flop. The ending of the series was underdeveloped, boring, and, honestly, stupid. Well...really...the entire series was underdeveloped, boring, and, honestly, stupid. Would not recommend. At all. Ever.</span>
  <a data-text-id="8273243179063041092" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText8686849627149312830" style="display:none">BLURB (TMR): When the doors of the lift crank open, the only thing Thomas can remember is his first name. But he’s not alone. He’s surrounded by boys who welcome him to the Glade, an encampment at the centre of a bizarre and terrible maze. <br />Like Thomas, the Gladers don’t know why or how they came to be there, or what’s happened to the world outside. All they know is that every morning when the walls slide back, they will risk everything to find out.<br /><br />WHAT I THOUGHT: I use to hate reading until I randomly bought the Maze Runner. I picked it up one day in a shop at the last minute, little did I know how incredible it was going to be. But I have to admit, I started reading it and I thought it was the worst book ever, I didn't get it at all, so I stopped reading it. Then about a month later I attempted to read it again and I got so into it. I couldn't put it down. It is literally such an amazing, jaw-dropping book. It's so dramatic and intense and each chapter ends on a cliff hanger which makes you want to read more. It has a superb storyline with characters that's you'll love and hate. It is a must read! And that's just the first book. The 2nd is The Scorch Trials, which if anything is even better than the Maze Runner. Lastly, there's The Death Cure. That book is so breath taking and it ends perfectly. I cried a lot after I read each book, and I don't cry often. That just shows what a huge effect these 3 books had on me. <br />There is also a prologue to this series called The Kill Order, which isn't all about the characters in The Maze Runner Series. It's more about how it all started. <br /><br />To sum that all up. If you haven't read this series... YOU HAVE TO!</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer9548765047866223436">I started reading these books after watching the maze runner movie. The books add a lot more intrigue and complex themes over its cinematic cousin. The pace and over all tone of the first book, 'the maze runner" was good over all but I fell like the pace sometimes outstripped the story. I was really really pleased with the second book 'the scorch trials' and I feel like it is my favorite of the 4. The story really begins to gain depth as Thomas' dreams start to flesh out his back story and as ne</span>
  <span id="freeText9548765047866223436" style="display:none">I started reading these books after watching the maze runner movie. The books add a lot more intrigue and complex themes over its cinematic cousin. The pace and over all tone of the first book, 'the maze runner" was good over all but I fell like the pace sometimes outstripped the story. I was really really pleased with the second book 'the scorch trials' and I feel like it is my favorite of the 4. The story really begins to gain depth as Thomas' dreams start to flesh out his back story and as new characters are added into the fray. The ending of the scorch trials left me a little dissatisfied because of the behavior of the main character and the short comings of his character that begin to show through his attitude and behavior towards his friend Theresa. "The death cure" was also a little unsatisfactory as the ending of the trilogy. The main characters continued anger and hatred, while understandable, detract a little from the story and never really let the full back story or resolution get flushed out in a satisfactory way. The prequel was interesting only in that it gives us background on the flare and the solar flares that ravaged the earth but I did not feel a connection with the main characters.<br /><br />Overall an interesting read that was gripping at times but overall left me a little dissatisfied.</span>
  <a data-text-id="9548765047866223436" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

  <span id="freeText13913051123153375623" style="display:none">I just finished listening to the 3 book Maze Runner series. Though the ratings are high for the book, I did not really enjoy the story. The book was definitely gripping, action packed and left you wanting to turn the pages, but I found the descriptions a little too grotesque and violent for my taste. I think a lot of the books success can be attributed to this 'shock' element. I also felt like the main character could be rather annoying at times, more towards the end of the second book and definitely throughout the third. I also did not like how the third book ended. I felt it was a hodge podge of things thrown together to make a climatic ending that didn't provide the closure it needed. Certain people also died which I thought did not contribute to the plot and instead left a void of 'huh'. Still, I read all three of the books, so I must have still liked them! They are just not a series I would necessarily promote, nor will I see the movie (and movies that come out after the first), too dark and violent! </span>

  <span id="freeText11089238951978073099" style="display:none">I've read the books as well as have seen the movies!<br />The movies are unlike the books though interesting, a better version I should say.<br />I've come through lots reviews about the books and the movies.<br />Being The Male Protogonist Stupid on some stuffs and Female a Betrayer.<br />Not excepting Thomas and Teresa and going on loving with Brenda and Thomas!<br />Dying of Newt (He's most enchanting character!)<br />About the end not satisfying and living questions!<br />So here it is—<br />On my opinion, a Best book is a Book which leaves the readers curious and asking for question in the end (which can be seen very clearly) asking for more. Leaving an unpredictable ending, weird even. Something for us make up in our minds. Not giving an conclusion through which readers can't go anywhere. A book with end for the readers to make up the 'what ifs' at some point. This series fits in it.<br />About The Protogonist- Thomas, well, he wanted to escape the past, the terrible memories. He trusted Teresa very much and sometimes when the super trustee betrayes us we just want to get away from it, cut all the ties. That's what Thomas was doing, trying to forgot! He didn't wanted his memories back as he kind of knew, his past days were all about WICKED, which is not something he wanted to be related to, anyhow, not even through memories. Terasa was a part of it, so was WICKED not something he wanted to do ant with. The role of WICKED in his life was more affecting in negative way than anything else, the memories will bring it back, there will be no escape than. <br />About, getting over Teresa's death so quickly is kind of natural, at the moment of breaking and tearing he needed comfort which he got eventually and he excepted that (we all do).<br />( Still, a part of me— super-stupid-freak he was, not forgiving Teresa ....And he kissed Brenda I so wanted to scratch his face and punch him in guts!!!! In the movie the moment was fine 'cause he expected Teresa instead of Brenda and he said so but in the book, damnnnnn!! I DO NOT LIKE HIM!!)<br /><br />The Female Protogonist- Teresa, whatever she did, she had reason and the reason are satisfying! To Save Thomas, she did recognized him. Felt a connection. There was nothing wrong, we hurt the one we love the most, it's natural, it's the Reality! I can't find myself to hate her, from the moment she showed up, I fell in love with her! She and Thomas had an emotional connection, a past connection, a long one, like the infinite line segment in mathematics! <br />She did what she had to, she needed to save Thomas and betrayel can save some one we love, it's not wrong. Her ways were itching, dislikeable, wrong but intentions were clean, admiring, right.<br />In the movie she just wanted to find a cure to save everyone. She doesn't think of herself going to the 'Safe Heaven', she got captivated with emotions, on regaining some past memories. Wanted to save everyone, even a part of her knowing she can't save everyone but can at least try, just like Thomas, wanted to save everyone he knew, even if he couldn't, he can try ("I can try"). There's nothing wrong with Teresa, emotionally captivated she was. <br />( Part of me wanted her to be with Thomas, they look so got together, I cried, still am when she died) Her death is worth remembering, she did it for Thomas. It shows her true care for him. It show She Is Not An Evil!!! She symbolises HOPE, to save the humanity, deep love for Thomas! There's nothing wrong with the death of one protogonist, there other books where hero or heroin dies, leaving the other all alone. It's frames reality! The author probably did this for the readers to Know that this happens, to give readers the positive side of Teresa. (She is beguiling)<br />Brenda— I don't really have anything to say about her ( I'M Teresa Fandom), I didn't gave much attention to her in books or movies. However, she's a legend. The way she is framed in the Movies, all fearless is amazing! In the book (I didn't gave much attention to her parts) she worked for WICKED but was only doing her job, she doesn't let the Graders escape in first place as perhaps she wanted to help go all the way to the WICKED base and bring it down. Have Thomas as she knew him from past and so wanted to be with him, nothing wrong, feelings! Can't do anything. And else (I didn't gave much attention, sorry Brenda Lovers).<br />(Part me- Her first show up and being touchy with The Protogonist, I was like "back off, he is Teresa's" or "Stay away, you are not his" either "I do not like you" ) (I screamed when Thomas wanted the times with her but smile and Dance around when He longed Teresa's presence)<br />Newt— (Do not ask me) He is enchanting!! I love him from the start. But The Author wanted to get into Protogonists head, making him lone and longing for comfort. His death symbolises the true reality of 'anything can happen' and 'life works with the principal of give and take' Thomas wanted to give lives to many others, losing the best friend true nature of negativity around. He was left alone, without Newt to work things on against the negatives. Creating the anger in Thomas against the wrong ones. Making the readers cursing over the lose giving them the feeling of emptiness, to go on and on with the book and engrained the book in mind for forever.<br />(Thomas, Minho, Newt— the best friends ever)<br />Ending— There's questions, curiosity, wanting of more, the ending is fine.<br />BUT, but..... Teresa's death, I don't like it! Newt, I do not like it!! <br />Ending left various things, it wanted to leave a mark in readers mind, and I think it did!<br />Thomas and Brenda ending up together, he just wanted comfort, which she gave.<br />( I love Thomesa!!!! This is what I want from the start!!! )<br />This series is amazing as it left the "why's" and "I'm engrained in your head, kinda flare type" part.<br />Appreciatable!!<br />Every author has it's own ways of writing and leaving a mark on readers minds, we should appreciate it! The thinking it needed first James Dashner to write such a plot can't be ignored!<br />Breath Taking Story line!!<br />Interesting plot!<br />I'LL DEFINITELY WRITE SOMETHING LIKE THAT TOO!!</span>

  <span id="freeText281877710631867930" style="display:none">I really enjoyed this series. When I first started reading the Maze Runner, to be honest, I wasn't really into it and I thought the way it was written was maybe a bit strange, however as I read the next books, each turn of the page it improved. In the end I was loving this series, and I thought the ending was PERFECT! I don't want to spoil anything, but I think that it was really realistic and a nice way to finish such a surprising and adventure packed series. I would recommend this gripping series to anyone likes adventure packed, and interesting book series! And remember that it improves on every turn of the page. The characters are addictive with every twist and turn of the plot! Absolutely fantastic James Dashner! </span>

The scripts must needs be an immense departure from the books from this point.       <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/28763051-audrey-rozman?shelf=middle-school-6-8">middle-school-6-8</a>,

          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer921931747" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11248972734161073703">I read this series in one week. The writing is not strong, nor is the storyline, however it is adventurous, gripping, and hard to put down! This book would not be featured in the classroom but could be used in book clubs or for side reading for students who are like the hunger games or the divergent series.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('BiLOGNsJb36Sk0rnwsKKO/aIrOuRtHruUuSmlDbJssDib5EzsdnOC962jc7OBhxTpI3+Qx/TUkk9yU9s2zw7MA==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('xOfHNXztz9RkkHpdmKs3udBVPDgsGTAtEiHOkMnrHvAgqpgeFj1uoSi1vXSUb6HRglBukKJ+GIp9DCdoJB6XAA==')})
  }
//]]>
